## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Cross-Org gRPC Service Definition Discovery

## Your Task

Find the gRPC service definitions that are shared between `envoyproxy/envoy` and `grpc/grpc`. Specifically: 1. In `envoyproxy/data-plane-api`, find all `.proto` files that define `service` declarations using `rpc` methods (the xDS service definitions). 2. In `grpc/grpc`, find the source files that implement the `grpc_health_v1.Health` service (the standard gRPC health checking protocol). Report the repo, file path, and service name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

It is expected that no new request is sent after a\\n64:   // response is received until the Envoy instance is ready to ACK/NACK the new\\n65:   // configuration. The LDS and CDS responses\\n77:   // will then imply a number of resources that need to be fetched via EDS/RDS,\\n78:   // which will be explicitly enumerated in ``resource_names``.\\n79:   repeated string resource_names = 3;\\n80: \\n81:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n82:   // Alternative to ``resource_names`` field that allows specifying dynamic\\n83:   // parameters along with each resource name. This\\n101:   // may be empty only if:\\n102:   //\\n103:   // * This is a non-persistent-stream xDS such as HTTP, or\\n104:   // * The client has not yet accepted an update in this xDS stream (unlike\\n105:   //   delta, where it is populated only for new explicit ACKs).\\n106:   //\\n107:   string response_nonce = 5;\\n108: \\n109:   // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.discovery.v3.DiscoveryResponse>`\\n110:   // failed to update configuration. The ``message`` field in ``error_details`` provides the Envoy\\n111:   // internal exception related to the failure. It is only intended for consumption during manual\\n112:   // debugging, the string provided is not guaranteed to be stable across Envoy versions.\\n113:   google.rpc.Status error_detail = 6;\\n114: }\\n115: \\n116: // [#next-free-field: 8]\\n117: message DiscoveryResponse {\\n118:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.DiscoveryResponse\\\";\\n119: \\n120:   // The version of the response data.\\n121:   string version_info = 1;\\n122: \\n123:   // The response resources. These resources are typed and depend on the API being called.\\n124:   repeated google.protobuf.Any resources = 2;\\n125: \\n126:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n127:   // Canary is used to support two Envoy command line flags:\\n128:   //\\n129:   // * ``--terminate-on-canary-transition-failure``. When set, Envoy is able to\\n130:   //   terminate if it detects that configuration is stuck at canary. Consider\\n131:   //   this example sequence of updates:\\n132:   //\\n133:   //   * Management server applies a canary config successfully.\\n134:   //   * Management server rolls back to a production config.\\n135:   //   * Envoy rejects the new production config.\\n136:   //\\n137:   //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\\n138:   //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\\n139:   //   clean slate.\\n140:   //\\n141:   // * ``--dry-run-canary``. When set, a canary response will never be applied, only\\n142:   //   validated via a dry run.\\n143:   //\\n144:   bool canary = 3;\\n145: \\n146:   // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\\n147:   // Must be consistent with the ``type_url`` in the 'resources' repeated Any (if non-empty).\\n148:   string type_url = 4;\\n149: \\n150:   // For gRPC based subscriptions, the nonce provides a way to explicitly ack a\\n151:   // specific ``DiscoveryResponse`` in a following ``DiscoveryRequest``. Additional\\n152:   // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\\n153:   // previous version on the stream prior to this ``DiscoveryResponse``, that were\\n154:   // unprocessed at response send time. The nonce allows the management server\\n155:   // to ignore any further ``DiscoveryRequests`` for the previous version until a\\n156:   // ``DiscoveryRequest`` bearing the nonce. The nonce is optional and is not\\n157:   // required for non-stream based xDS implementations.\\n158:   string nonce = 5;\\n159: \\n160:   // The control plane instance that sent the response.\\n161:   config.core.v3.ControlPlane control_plane = 6;\\n162: \\n163:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n164:   // Errors associated with specific resources. Clients are expected to\\n165:   // remember the most recent error for a given resource across responses;\\n166:   // the error condition is not considered to be cleared until a response is\\n167:   // received that contains the resource in the 'resources' field.\\n168:   repeated ResourceError resource_errors = 7;\\n169: }\\n170: \\n171: // DeltaDiscoveryRequest and DeltaDiscoveryResponse are used in a new gRPC\\n172: // endpoint for Delta xDS.\\n173: //\\n174: // With Delta xDS, the DeltaDiscoveryResponses do not need to include a full\\n175: // snapshot of the tracked resources. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\\n176: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\\n177: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\\n178: // the resource granularity.\\n179: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\\n180: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\\n181: // connected to it.\\n182: //\\n183: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\\n184: // ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` to a ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` ACK or NACK.\\n185: // Optionally, a response message level ``system_version_info`` is present for\\n186: // debugging purposes only.\\n187: //\\n188: // ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` plays two independent roles. Any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``\\n189: // can be either or both of:\\n190: //\\n191: // * Informing the server of what resources the client has gained/lost interest in\\n192: //   (using ``resource_names_subscribe`` and ``resource_names_unsubscribe``), or\\n193: // * (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from the server (using ``response_nonce``,\\n194: //   with presence of ``error_detail`` making it a NACK).\\n195: //\\n196: // Additionally, the first message (for a given ``type_url``) of a reconnected gRPC stream\\n197: // has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\\n198: // that the client already possesses, using the ``initial_resource_versions`` field.\\n199: //\\n200: // As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\\n201: // all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by ``type_url``:\\n202: // a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\\n203: // In particular, ``initial_resource_versions`` being sent at the \\\"start\\\" of every\\n204: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each ``type_url``, each with its own\\n205: // ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n206: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n207: message DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\\n208:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\\\";\\n209: \\n210:   // The node making the request.\\n211:   config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\\n212: \\n213:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\\n214:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. This does not need to be set if\\n215:   // resources are only referenced via ``xds_resource_subscribe`` and\\n216:   // ``xds_resources_unsubscribe``.\\n217:   string type_url = 2;\\n218: \\n219:   // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\\n220:   // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\\n221:   // All resource names in the ``resource_names_subscribe`` list are added to the\\n222:   // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the ``resource_names_unsubscribe``\\n223:   // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\\n224:   //\\n225:   // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty ``resource_names_subscribe`` or\\n226:   // ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` list simply means that no resources are to be\\n227:   // added or removed to the resource list.\\n228:   // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\\n229:   // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\\n230:   //\\n231:   // .. note::\\n232:   //   The server must respond with all resources listed in ``resource_names_subscribe``,\\n233:   //   even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\\n234:   //   the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\\n235:   //   to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\\n236:   //\\n237:   // These two fields can be set in any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``, including ACKs\\n238:   // and ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n239:   //\\n240:   // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\\n241:   repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\\n242: \\n243:   // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\\n244:   repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\\n245: \\n246:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n247:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_subscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\\n248:   // along with each resource name.\\n249:   //\\n250:   // .. note::\\n251:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\\n252:   //   in ``resource_names_subscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_subscribe``.\\n253:   //\\n254:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_subscribe = 8;\\n255: \\n256:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n257:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\\n258:   // along with each resource name.\\n259:   //\\n260:   // .. note::\\n261:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\\n262:   //   in ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_unsubscribe``.\\n263:   //\\n264:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_unsubscribe = 9;\\n265: \\n266:   // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\\n267:   // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\\n268:   // It will not be populated:\\n269:   //\\n270:   // * In the very first stream of a session, since the client will not yet have any resources.\\n271:   // * In any message after the first in a stream (for a given ``type_url``), since the server will\\n272:   //   already be correctly tracking the client's state.\\n273:   //\\n274:   // (In ADS, the first message ``of each type_url`` of a reconnected stream populates this map.)\\n275:   // The map's keys are names of xDS resources known to the When set, Envoy is able to\n130:   //   terminate if it detects that configuration is stuck at canary. Consider\n131:   //   this example sequence of updates:\n132:   //\n133:   //   * Management server applies a canary config successfully.\n134:   //   * Management server rolls back to a production config.\n135:   //   * Envoy rejects the new production config.\n136:   //\n137:   //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\n138:   //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\n139:   //   clean slate.\n140:   //\n141:   // * ``--dry-run-canary``. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\n176: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\n177: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\n178: // the resource granularity.\n179: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\n180: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\n181: // connected to it.\n182: //\n183: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\n184: // ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` to a ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` ACK or NACK.\n185: // Optionally, a response message level ``system_version_info`` is present for\n186: // debugging purposes only.\n187: //\n188: // ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` plays two independent roles. Any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``\n189: // can be either or both of:\n190: //\n191: // * Informing the server of what resources the client has gained/lost interest in\n192: //   (using ``resource_names_subscribe`` and ``resource_names_unsubscribe``), or\n193: // * (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from the server (using ``response_nonce``,\n194: //   with presence of ``error_detail`` making it a NACK).\n195: //\n196: // Additionally, the first message (for a given ``type_url``) of a reconnected gRPC stream\n197: // has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\n198: // that the client already possesses, using the ``initial_resource_versions`` field.\n199: //\n200: // As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\n201: // all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by ``type_url``:\n202: // a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\n203: // In particular, ``initial_resource_versions`` being sent at the \"start\" of every\n204: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each ``type_url``, each with its own\n205: // ``initial_resource_versions``.\n206: // [#next-free-field: 10]\n207: message DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\n208:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\";\n209: \n210:   // The node making the request.\n211:   config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\n212: \n213:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\n214:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\\n44: //\\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does.     "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.service.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/type/v3/http_status.proto\";\n8: \n9: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n10: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n11: \n12: import \"xds/annotations/v3/status.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"envoy/annotations/deprecation.proto\";\n15: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n16: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n17: \n18: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.ext_proc.v3\";\n19: option java_outer_classname = \"ExternalProcessorProto\";\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\n21: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External processing service]\n25: \n26: // A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses as part of a filter chain.\n27: // The overall external processing protocol works like this:\n28: //\n29: // 1. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\n44: //\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does. Unlike the\\n24: // HTTP External Processing filter, this service operates at the TCP/UDP level,\\n25: // providing access to raw network data.\\n26: //\\n27: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service that can:\\n28: //\\n29: // 1. Inspect network traffic in both directions (client->server and server->client)\\n30: // 2. Modify the payload data\\n31: // 3. Control connection lifecycle (continue, close gracefully, or reset)\\n32: //\\n33: // Use cases include:\\n34: //\\n35: // 1. Custom protocol inspection and modification\\n36: // 2. Advanced traffic manipulation\\n37: // 3. Security scanning and filtering\\n38: // 4. Dynamic connection management\\n39: //\\n40: // The service uses a bidirectional gRPC stream, maintaining state throughout\\n41: // the connection lifetime while allowing asynchronous processing.\\n42: \\n43: // NetworkExternalProcessor service defines the contract between Envoy and\\n44: // external processing servers for L4 network traffic.\\n45: service NetworkExternalProcessor {\\n46:   // Process establishes a bidirectional stream between Envoy and the external\\n47:   // processing server.     "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.service.network_ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n6: \n7: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n8: \n9: import \"xds/annotations/v3/status.proto\";\n10: \n11: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n12: \n13: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.network_ext_proc.v3\";\n14: option java_outer_classname = \"NetworkExternalProcessorProto\";\n15: option java_multiple_files = true;\n16: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/network_ext_proc/v3;network_ext_procv3\";\n17: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n18: option (xds.annotations.v3.file_status).work_in_progress = true;\n19: \n20: // [#protodoc-title: Network External Processing Service]\n21: \n22: // The Network External Processing filter allows an external service to dynamically\n23: // interact with and modify L4 network traffic passing through Envoy. Unlike the\n24: // HTTP External Processing filter, this service operates at the TCP/UDP level,\n25: // providing access to raw network data.\n26: //\n27: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service that can:\n28: //\n29: // 1. Inspect network traffic in both directions (client->server and server->client)\n30: // 2. Modify the payload data\n31: // 3. Control connection lifecycle (continue, close gracefully, or reset)\n32: //\n33: // Use cases include:\n34: //\n35: // 1. Custom protocol inspection and modification\n36: // 2. Advanced traffic manipulation\n37: // 3. Security scanning and filtering\n38: // 4. Dynamic connection management\n39: //\n40: // The service uses a bidirectional gRPC stream, maintaining state throughout\n41: // the connection lifetime while allowing asynchronous processing.\n42: \n43: // NetworkExternalProcessor service defines the contract between Envoy and\n44: // external processing servers for L4 network traffic.\n45: service NetworkExternalProcessor {\n46:   // Process establishes a bidirectional stream between Envoy and the external\n47:   // processing server. Envoy sends ProcessingRequests containing network data\n48:   // and the server responds with ProcessingResponses containing processing\n49:   // decisions and potentially modified data.\n50:   //\n51:   // The server should handle processing timeout properly to avoid blocking\n52:   // network traffic for extended periods. Any uncaught exceptions will\n53:   // be treated as errors and will terminate the stream.\n54:   //\n55:   // Implementation note: The server should process requests in the order\n56:   // they are received to maintain proper sequencing of network traffic.\n57:   rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\n58:   }\n59: }\n60: \n61: // The payload data from network layer\n62: message Data {\n63:   // The raw payload data\n64:   bytes data = 1;\n65: \n66:   // Indicates whether this is the last data frame in the current direction.\n67:   // The external processor should still respond to this message even\n68:   // if there is no more data expected in this direction.\n69:   bool end_of_stream = 2;\n70: }\n71: \n72: // ProcessingRequest contains data sent from Envoy to the external processing server.\n73: // Each request contains either read data (from client) or write data (to client)\n74: // along with optional metadata.\n75: message ProcessingRequest {\n76:   // ReadData contains the network data intercepted in the request path (client to server).\n77:   // This is sent to the external processor when data arrives from the downstream client.\n78:   // If this is set, write_data should not be set.\n79:   Data read_data = 1;\n80: \n81:   // WriteData contains the network data intercepted in the response path (server to client).\n82:   // This is sent to the external processor when data arrives from the upstream server.\n83:   // If this is set, read_data should not be set.\n84:   Data write_data = 2;\n85: \n86:   // Optional metadata associated with the request.\n87:   // This can include connection properties, filter configuration, and any other\n88:   // contextual information that might be useful for processing decisions.\n89:   //\n90:   // The metadata is not automatically propagated from request to response.\n91:   // The external processor must include any needed metadata in its response.\n92:   config.core.v3.Metadata metadata = 3;\n93: }\n94: \n95: // ProcessingResponse contains the response from the external processing server to Envoy.\n96: // Each response corresponds to a ProcessingRequest and indicates how the network\n97: // traffic should be handled.\n98: // [#next-free-field: 6]\n99: message ProcessingResponse {\n100:   // DataProcessedStatus indicates whether the data was modified by the external processor.\n101:   enum DataProcessedStatus {\n102:     // The data processed status is unknown.\n103:     UNKNOWN = 0;\n104: \n105:     // The data remains unchanged. Envoy will use the original data.\n106:     // This is useful when the processor only wants to inspect but not modify the traffic.\n107:     UNMODIFIED = 1;\n108: \n109:     // The data has been modified. Envoy will use the modified data provided in the response.\n110:     // This allows the processor to transform the network traffic as needed.\n111:     MODIFIED = 2;\n112:   }\n113: \n114:   // ConnectionStatus determines what happens to the connection after processing.\n115:   enum ConnectionStatus {\n116:     // Continue normal processing of the connection.\n117:     // This is the default behavior and allows traffic to flow normally.\n118:     CONTINUE = 0;\n119: \n120:     // Close the connection with normal TCP FIN.\n121:     // This allows for clean connection termination with a normal close sequence.\n122:     // Any buffered data will be sent before closing.\n123:     CLOSE = 1;\n124: \n125:     // Immediately reset the connection with TCP RST.\n126:     // This forcibly terminates the connection without a clean shutdown,\n127:     // discarding any buffered data. Use this for security-critical situations\n128:     // or when immediate termination is required.\n129:     CLOSE_RST = 2;\n130:   }\n131: \n132:   // The processed ReadData containing potentially modified data for the request path.\n133:   // This should be sent in response to a ProcessingRequest with read_data, and the\n134:   // previous data in ProcessingRequest will be replaced by the new data in Envoy's data plane.\n135:   // If this is set, write_data should not be set.\n136:   Data read_data = 1;\n137: \n138:   // The processed WriteData containing potentially modified data for the response path.\n139:   // This should be sent in response to a ProcessingRequest with write_data, and the\n140:   // previous data in ProcessingRequest will be replaced by the new data in Envoy's data plane.\n141:   // If this is set, read_data should not be set.\n142:   Data write_data = 2;\n143: \n144:   // Indicates whether the data was modified or not.\n145:   // This is mandatory and tells Envoy whether to use the original or modified data.\n146:   DataProcessedStatus data_processing_status = 3;\n147: \n148:   // Optional: Determines the connection behavior after processing.\n149:   // If not specified, CONTINUE is assumed, and the connection proceeds normally.\n150:   // Use CLOSE or CLOSE_RST to terminate the connection based on processing results.\n151:   ConnectionStatus connection_status = 4;\n152: \n153:   // Optional metadata associated with the request.\n154:   // This can include connection properties, filter configuration, and any other\n155:   // contextual information that might be useful for processing decisions.\n156:   //\n157:   // The metadata is not automatically propagated from request to response.\n158:   // The external processor must include any needed metadata in its response.\n159:   google.protobuf.Struct dynamic_metadata = 5;\n160: }\n161: ",

The service will aggregate the usage reports\\n25: // from multiple data plane instances, and distribute Rate Limit Assignments to each instance\\n26: // based on its business logic. The logic is outside of the scope of the protocol API.\\n27: //\\n28: // The protocol is designed as a streaming-first API. It utilizes watch-like subscription model.\\n29: // The data plane groups requests into Quota Buckets as directed by the filter config,\\n30: // and periodically reports them to the RLQS server along with the Bucket identifier, :ref:`BucketId\\n31: // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.BucketId>`. Once RLQS server has collected enough\\n32: // reports to make a decision, it'll send back the assignment with the rate limiting instructions.\\n33: //\\n34: // The first report sent by the data plane is interpreted by the RLQS server as a \\\"watch\\\" request,\\n35: // indicating that the data plane instance is interested in receiving further updates for the\\n36: // ``BucketId``. From then on, RLQS server may push assignments to this instance at will, even if\\n37: // the instance is not sending usage reports. It's the responsibility of the RLQS server\\n38: // to determine when the data plane instance didn't send ``BucketId`` reports for too long,\\n39: // and to respond with the :ref:`AbandonAction\\n40: // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`,\\n41: // indicating that the server has now stopped sending quota assignments for the ``BucketId`` bucket,\\n42: // and the data plane instance should :ref:`abandon\\n43: // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.abandon_action>`\\n44: // it.\\n45: //\\n46: // If for any reason the RLQS client doesn't receive the initial assignment for the reported bucket,\\n47: // in order to prevent memory exhaustion, the data plane will limit the time such bucket\\n48: // is retained. The exact time to wait for the initial assignment is chosen by the filter,\\n49: // and may vary based on the implementation.\\n50: // Once the duration ends, the data plane will stop reporting bucket usage, reject any enqueued\\n51: // requests, and purge the bucket from the memory. Subsequent requests matched into the bucket\\n52: // will re-initialize the bucket in the \\\"no assignment\\\" state, restarting the reports.\\n53: //\\n54: // Refer to Rate Limit Quota :ref:`configuration overview <config_http_filters_rate_limit_quota>`\\n55: // for further details.\\n56: \\n57: // Defines the Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS).\\n58: service RateLimitQuotaService {\\n59:   // Main communication channel: the data plane sends usage reports to the RLQS server,\\n60:   // and the server asynchronously responding with the assignments.\\n61:   rpc StreamRateLimitQuotas(stream RateLimitQuotaUsageReports)\\n62:       returns (stream RateLimitQuotaResponse) {\\n63:   }\\n64: }\\n65: \\n66: message RateLimitQuotaUsageReports {\\n67:   // The usage report for a bucket.\\n68:   //\\n69:   // .. note::\\n70:   //   Note that the first report sent for a ``BucketId`` indicates to the RLQS server that\\n71:   //   the RLQS client is subscribing for the future assignments for this ``BucketId``.\\n72:   message BucketQuotaUsage {\\n73:     // ``BucketId`` for which request quota usage is reported.\\n74:     BucketId bucket_id = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n75: \\n76:     // Time elapsed since the last report.\\n77:     google.protobuf.Duration time_elapsed = 2 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n78:       required: true\\n79:       gt {}\\n80:     }];\\n81: \\n82:     // Requests the data plane has allowed through.\\n83:     uint64 num_requests_allowed = 3;\\n84: \\n85:     // Requests throttled.\\n86:     uint64 num_requests_denied = 4;\\n87:   }\\n88: \\n89:   // All quota requests must specify the domain. This enables sharing the quota\\n90:   // server between different applications without fear of overlap.\\n91:   // E.g., \\\"envoy\\\".\\n92:   //\\n93:   // Should only be provided in the first report, all subsequent messages on the same\\n94:   // stream are considered to be in the same domain. In case the domain needs to be\\n95:   // changes, close the stream, and reopen a new one with the different domain.\\n96:   string domain = 1 [(validate.rules).string = {min_len: 1}];\\n97: \\n98:   // A list of quota usage reports. The list is processed by the RLQS server in the same order\\n99:   // it's provided by the client.\\n100:   repeated BucketQuotaUsage bucket_quota_usages = 2 [(validate.rules).repeated = {min_items: 1}];\\n101: }\\n102: \\n103: message RateLimitQuotaResponse {\\n104:   // Commands the data plane to apply one of the actions to the bucket with the\\n105:   // :ref:`bucket_id <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\\n106:   message BucketAction {\\n107:     // Quota assignment for the bucket. Configures the rate limiting strategy and the duration\\n108:     // for the given :ref:`bucket_id\\n109:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\\n110:     //\\n111:     // **Applying the first assignment to the bucket**\\n112:     //\\n113:     // Once the data plane receives the ``QuotaAssignmentAction``, it must send the current usage\\n114:     // report for the bucket, and start rate limiting requests matched into the bucket\\n115:     // using the strategy configured in the :ref:`rate_limit_strategy\\n116:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.rate_limit_strategy>`\\n117:     // field. The assignment becomes bucket's ``active`` assignment.\\n118:     //\\n119:     // **Expiring the assignment**\\n120:     //\\n121:     // The duration of the assignment defined in the :ref:`assignment_time_to_live\\n122:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.assignment_time_to_live>`\\n123:     // field. When the duration runs off, the assignment is ``expired``, and no longer ``active``.\\n124:     // The data plane should stop applying the rate limiting strategy to the bucket, and transition\\n125:     // the bucket to the \\\"expired assignment\\\" state. This activates the behavior configured in the\\n126:     // :ref:`expired_assignment_behavior <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.expired_assignment_behavior>`\\n127:     // field.\\n128:     //\\n129:     // **Replacing the assignment**\\n130:     //\\n131:     // * If the rate limiting strategy is different from bucket's ``active`` assignment, or\\n132:     //   the current bucket assignment is ``expired``, the data plane must immediately\\n133:     //   end the current assignment, report the bucket usage, and apply the new assignment.\\n134:     //   The new assignment becomes bucket's ``active`` assignment.\\n135:     // * If the rate limiting strategy is the same as the bucket's ``active`` (not ``expired``)\\n136:     //   assignment, the data plane should extend the duration of the ``active`` assignment\\n137:     //   for the duration of the new assignment provided in the :ref:`assignment_time_to_live\\n138:     //   <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.assignment_time_to_live>`\\n139:     //   field. The ``active`` assignment is considered unchanged.\\n140:     message QuotaAssignmentAction {\\n141:       // A duration after which the assignment is be considered ``expired``. The process of the\\n142:       // expiration is described :ref:`above\\n143:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`.\\n144:       //\\n145:       // * If unset, the assignment has no expiration date.\\n146:       // * If set to ``0``, the assignment expires immediately, forcing the client into the\\n147:       //   :ref:`\\\"expired assignment\\\"\\n148:       //   <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.ExpiredAssignmentBehavior.expired_assignment_behavior_timeout>`\\n149:       //   state. This may be used by the RLQS server in cases when it needs clients to proactively\\n150:       //   fall back to the pre-configured :ref:`ExpiredAssignmentBehavior\\n151:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.ExpiredAssignmentBehavior>`,\\n152:       //   f.e. before the server going into restart.\\n153:       //\\n154:       // .. attention::\\n155:       //   Note that :ref:`expiring\\n156:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`\\n157:       //   the assignment is not the same as :ref:`abandoning\\n158:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`\\n159:       //   the assignment. While expiring the assignment just transitions the bucket to\\n160:       //   the \\\"expired assignment\\\" state; abandoning the assignment completely erases\\n161:       //   the bucket from the data plane memory, and stops the usage reports.\\n162:       google.protobuf.Duration assignment_time_to_live = 2 [(validate.rules).duration = {gte {}}];\\n163: \\n164:       // Configures the local rate limiter for the request matched to the bucket.\\n165:       // If not set, allow all requests.\\n166:       type.v3.RateLimitStrategy rate_limit_strategy = 3;\\n167:     }\\n168: \\n169:     // Abandon action for the bucket. Indicates that the RLQS server will no longer be\\n170:     // sending updates for the given :ref:`bucket_id\\n171:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\\n172:     //\\n173:     // If no requests are reported for a bucket, after some time the server considers the bucket\\n174:     // inactive. The server stops tracking the bucket, and instructs the the data plane to abandon\\n175:     // the bucket via this message.\\n176:     //\\n177:     // **Abandoning the assignment**\\n178:     //\\n179:     // The data plane is to erase the bucket (including its usage data) from the memory.\\n180:     // It should stop tracking the bucket, and stop reporting its usage. This effectively resets\\n181:     // the data plane to the state prior to matching the first request into the bucket.\\n182:     //\\n183:     // **Restarting the subscription**\\n184:     //\\n185:     // If a new request is matched into a bucket previously abandoned, the data plane must behave\\n186:     // as if it has never tracked the bucket, and it's the first request matched into it:\\n187:     //\\n188:     // 1. The process of :ref:`subscription and reporting\\n189:     //    <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.reporting_interval>`\\n190:     //    starts from the beginning.\\n191:     //\\n192:     // 2. The bucket transitions to the :ref:`\\\"no assignment\\\"\\n193:     //    <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.no_assignment_behavior>`\\n194:     //    state.\\n195:     //\\n196:     // 3. Once the new assignment is received, it's applied per\\n197:     //    \\\"Applying the first assignment to the bucket\\\" section of the :ref:`QuotaAssignmentAction\\n198:     //    <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`.\\n199:     message AbandonAction {\\n200:     }\\n201: \\n202:     // ``BucketId`` for which request the action is applied.\\n203:     BucketId bucket_id = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n204: \\n205:     oneof bucket_action {\\n206:       option (validate.required) = true;\\n207: \\n208:       // Apply the quota assignment to the bucket.\\n209:       //\\n210:       // Commands the data plane to apply a rate limiting strategy to the bucket.\\n211:       // The process of applying and expiring the rate limiting strategy is detailed in the\\n212:       // :ref:`QuotaAssignmentAction\\n213:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`\\n214:       // message.\\n215:       QuotaAssignmentAction quota_assignment_action = 2;\\n216: \\n217:       // Abandon the bucket.\\n218:       //\\n219:       // Commands the data plane to abandon the bucket.\\n220:       // The process of abandoning the bucket is described in the :ref:`AbandonAction\\n221:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`\\n222:       // message.\\n223:       AbandonAction abandon_action = 3;\\n224:     }\\n225:   }\\n226: \\n227:   // An ordered list of actions to be applied to the buckets. The actions are applied in the\\n228:   // given order, from top to bottom.\\n229:   repeated BucketAction bucket_action = 1 [(validate.rules).repeated = {min_items: 1}];\\n230: }\\n231: \\n232: // The identifier for the bucket. It's the responsibility of the RLQS server\n38: // to determine when the data plane instance didn't send ``BucketId`` reports for too long,\n39: // and to respond with the :ref:`AbandonAction\n40: // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`,\n41: // indicating that the server has now stopped sending quota assignments for the ``BucketId`` bucket,\n42: // and the data plane instance should :ref:`abandon\n43: // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.abandon_action>`\n44: // it.\n45: //\n46: // If for any reason the RLQS client doesn't receive the initial assignment for the reported bucket,\n47: // in order to prevent memory exhaustion, the data plane will limit the time such bucket\n48: // is retained. The exact time to wait for the initial assignment is chosen by the filter,\n49: // and may vary based on the implementation.\n50: // Once the duration ends, the data plane will stop reporting bucket usage, reject any enqueued\n51: // requests, and purge the bucket from the memory. Subsequent requests matched into the bucket\n52: // will re-initialize the bucket in the \"no assignment\" state, restarting the reports.\n53: //\n54: // Refer to Rate Limit Quota :ref:`configuration overview <config_http_filters_rate_limit_quota>`\n55: // for further details.\n56: \n57: // Defines the Rate Limit Quota Service (RLQS).\n58: service RateLimitQuotaService {\n59:   // Main communication channel: the data plane sends usage reports to the RLQS server,\n60:   // and the server asynchronously responding with the assignments.\n61:   rpc StreamRateLimitQuotas(stream RateLimitQuotaUsageReports)\n62:       returns (stream RateLimitQuotaResponse) {\n63:   }\n64: }\n65: \n66: message RateLimitQuotaUsageReports {\n67:   // The usage report for a bucket.\n68:   //\n69:   // .. note::\n70:   //   Note that the first report sent for a ``BucketId`` indicates to the RLQS server that\n71:   //   the RLQS client is subscribing for the future assignments for this ``BucketId``.\n72:   message BucketQuotaUsage {\n73:     // ``BucketId`` for which request quota usage is reported.\n74:     BucketId bucket_id = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n75: \n76:     // Time elapsed since the last report.\n77:     google.protobuf.Duration time_elapsed = 2 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n78:       required: true\n79:       gt {}\n80:     }];\n81: \n82:     // Requests the data plane has allowed through.\n83:     uint64 num_requests_allowed = 3;\n84: \n85:     // Requests throttled.\n86:     uint64 num_requests_denied = 4;\n87:   }\n88: \n89:   // All quota requests must specify the domain. This enables sharing the quota\n90:   // server between different applications without fear of overlap.\n91:   // E.g., \"envoy\".\n92:   //\n93:   // Should only be provided in the first report, all subsequent messages on the same\n94:   // stream are considered to be in the same domain. In case the domain needs to be\n95:   // changes, close the stream, and reopen a new one with the different domain.\n96:   string domain = 1 [(validate.rules).string = {min_len: 1}];\n97: \n98:   // A list of quota usage reports. The list is processed by the RLQS server in the same order\n99:   // it's provided by the client.\n100:   repeated BucketQuotaUsage bucket_quota_usages = 2 [(validate.rules).repeated = {min_items: 1}];\n101: }\n102: \n103: message RateLimitQuotaResponse {\n104:   // Commands the data plane to apply one of the actions to the bucket with the\n105:   // :ref:`bucket_id <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\n106:   message BucketAction {\n107:     // Quota assignment for the bucket. Configures the rate limiting strategy and the duration\n108:     // for the given :ref:`bucket_id\n109:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\n110:     //\n111:     // **Applying the first assignment to the bucket**\n112:     //\n113:     // Once the data plane receives the ``QuotaAssignmentAction``, it must send the current usage\n114:     // report for the bucket, and start rate limiting requests matched into the bucket\n115:     // using the strategy configured in the :ref:`rate_limit_strategy\n116:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.rate_limit_strategy>`\n117:     // field. The assignment becomes bucket's ``active`` assignment.\n118:     //\n119:     // **Expiring the assignment**\n120:     //\n121:     // The duration of the assignment defined in the :ref:`assignment_time_to_live\n122:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.assignment_time_to_live>`\n123:     // field. When the duration runs off, the assignment is ``expired``, and no longer ``active``.\n124:     // The data plane should stop applying the rate limiting strategy to the bucket, and transition\n125:     // the bucket to the \"expired assignment\" state. This activates the behavior configured in the\n126:     // :ref:`expired_assignment_behavior <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.expired_assignment_behavior>`\n127:     // field.\n128:     //\n129:     // **Replacing the assignment**\n130:     //\n131:     // * If the rate limiting strategy is different from bucket's ``active`` assignment, or\n132:     //   the current bucket assignment is ``expired``, the data plane must immediately\n133:     //   end the current assignment, report the bucket usage, and apply the new assignment.\n134:     //   The new assignment becomes bucket's ``active`` assignment.\n135:     // * If the rate limiting strategy is the same as the bucket's ``active`` (not ``expired``)\n136:     //   assignment, the data plane should extend the duration of the ``active`` assignment\n137:     //   for the duration of the new assignment provided in the :ref:`assignment_time_to_live\n138:     //   <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction.assignment_time_to_live>`\n139:     //   field. The ``active`` assignment is considered unchanged.\n140:     message QuotaAssignmentAction {\n141:       // A duration after which the assignment is be considered ``expired``. The process of the\n142:       // expiration is described :ref:`above\n143:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`.\n144:       //\n145:       // * If unset, the assignment has no expiration date.\n146:       // * If set to ``0``, the assignment expires immediately, forcing the client into the\n147:       //   :ref:`\"expired assignment\"\n148:       //   <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.ExpiredAssignmentBehavior.expired_assignment_behavior_timeout>`\n149:       //   state. This may be used by the RLQS server in cases when it needs clients to proactively\n150:       //   fall back to the pre-configured :ref:`ExpiredAssignmentBehavior\n151:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.ExpiredAssignmentBehavior>`,\n152:       //   f.e. before the server going into restart.\n153:       //\n154:       // .. attention::\n155:       //   Note that :ref:`expiring\n156:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`\n157:       //   the assignment is not the same as :ref:`abandoning\n158:       //   <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`\n159:       //   the assignment. While expiring the assignment just transitions the bucket to\n160:       //   the \"expired assignment\" state; abandoning the assignment completely erases\n161:       //   the bucket from the data plane memory, and stops the usage reports.\n162:       google.protobuf.Duration assignment_time_to_live = 2 [(validate.rules).duration = {gte {}}];\n163: \n164:       // Configures the local rate limiter for the request matched to the bucket.\n165:       // If not set, allow all requests.\n166:       type.v3.RateLimitStrategy rate_limit_strategy = 3;\n167:     }\n168: \n169:     // Abandon action for the bucket. Indicates that the RLQS server will no longer be\n170:     // sending updates for the given :ref:`bucket_id\n171:     // <envoy_v3_api_field_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.bucket_id>`.\n172:     //\n173:     // If no requests are reported for a bucket, after some time the server considers the bucket\n174:     // inactive. The server stops tracking the bucket, and instructs the the data plane to abandon\n175:     // the bucket via this message.\n176:     //\n177:     // **Abandoning the assignment**\n178:     //\n179:     // The data plane is to erase the bucket (including its usage data) from the memory.\n180:     // It should stop tracking the bucket, and stop reporting its usage. This effectively resets\n181:     // the data plane to the state prior to matching the first request into the bucket.\n182:     //\n183:     // **Restarting the subscription**\n184:     //\n185:     // If a new request is matched into a bucket previously abandoned, the data plane must behave\n186:     // as if it has never tracked the bucket, and it's the first request matched into it:\n187:     //\n188:     // 1. The process of :ref:`subscription and reporting\n189:     //    <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.reporting_interval>`\n190:     //    starts from the beginning.\n191:     //\n192:     // 2. The bucket transitions to the :ref:`\"no assignment\"\n193:     //    <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaBucketSettings.no_assignment_behavior>`\n194:     //    state.\n195:     //\n196:     // 3. Once the new assignment is received, it's applied per\n197:     //    \"Applying the first assignment to the bucket\" section of the :ref:`QuotaAssignmentAction\n198:     //    <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`.\n199:     message AbandonAction {\n200:     }\n201: \n202:     // ``BucketId`` for which request the action is applied.\n203:     BucketId bucket_id = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n204: \n205:     oneof bucket_action {\n206:       option (validate.required) = true;\n207: \n208:       // Apply the quota assignment to the bucket.\n209:       //\n210:       // Commands the data plane to apply a rate limiting strategy to the bucket.\n211:       // The process of applying and expiring the rate limiting strategy is detailed in the\n212:       // :ref:`QuotaAssignmentAction\n213:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.QuotaAssignmentAction>`\n214:       // message.\n215:       QuotaAssignmentAction quota_assignment_action = 2;\n216: \n217:       // Abandon the bucket.\n218:       //\n219:       // Commands the data plane to abandon the bucket.\n220:       // The process of abandoning the bucket is described in the :ref:`AbandonAction\n221:       // <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.rate_limit_quota.v3.RateLimitQuotaResponse.BucketAction.AbandonAction>`\n222:       // message.\n223:       AbandonAction abandon_action = 3;\n224:     }\n225:   }\n226: \n227:   // An ordered list of actions to be applied to the buckets. The actions are applied in the\n228:   // given order, from top to bottom.\n229:   repeated BucketAction bucket_action = 1 [(validate.rules).repeated = {min_items: 1}];\n230: }\n231: \n232: // The identifier for the bucket. **SecretDiscoveryService** (envoy/service/discovery/v2/sds.proto, envoy/service/secret/v3/sds.proto): SDS for secret management\\n\\n**Extended Services:**\\n- **AccessLogService** (envoy/service/accesslog/v2/als.proto, envoy/service/accesslog/v3/als.proto): For streaming access logs\\n- **Authorization** (envoy/service/auth/v2/external_auth.proto, envoy/service/auth/v3/external_auth.proto): External authorization service\\n- **EventReportingService** (envoy/service/event_reporting/v3/event_reporting_service.proto): Event streaming\\n- **ExternalProcessor** (envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto): HTTP external processing\\n- **ExtensionConfigDiscoveryService** (envoy/service/extension/v3/config_discovery.proto): ECDS for filter configuration\\n- **HealthDiscoveryService** (envoy/service/discovery/v2/hds.proto, envoy/service/health/v3/hds.proto): Health status reporting\\n- **LoadReportingService** (envoy/service/load_stats/v3/lrs.proto): LRS for load reporting\\n- **MetricsService** (envoy/service/metrics/v2/metrics_service.proto, envoy/service/metrics/v3/metrics_service.proto): Metrics streaming\\n- **NetworkExternalProcessor** (envoy/service/network_ext_proc/v3/network_external_processor.proto): Network-level external processing\\n- **RateLimitService** (envoy/service/ratelimit/v2/rls.proto, envoy/service/ratelimit/v3/rls.proto): Global rate limiting\\n- **RateLimitQuotaService** (envoy/service/rate_limit_quota/v3/rlqs.proto): Rate limit quota management\\n- **RedisProxyExternalAuth** (envoy/service/redis_auth/v3/redis_external_auth.proto): Redis external authentication\\n- **RuntimeDiscoveryService** (envoy/service/discovery/v2/rtds.proto, Comprehensive test implementation\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\nThe Envoy xDS services are domain-specific discovery and control plane protocols designed for proxy configuration management, while the gRPC Health service is a universal health-checking mechanism defined in grpc-proto and implemented across all major gRPC language implementations.
